## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction, where the rate typically depends on the current concentration A raised to some power (reaction order). Time t may appear explicitly in non-autonomous systems such as photolysis or externally driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law dependence on concentration)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction driving toward equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (photolysis or time-varying rate constant)
- Fractional order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with baseline)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Parallel pathway model: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (two competing reaction pathways)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (linearly changing rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power-law dependence on concentration → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power (e.g., A**2 implies bimolecular)
- Negative rate constant (c0 < 0) → reactant consumption/decay; positive → product formation or autocatalysis
- Rational function of concentration (A/(c+A)) → enzyme or surface-catalyzed mechanism with saturation at high concentration
- Product of concentration and (constant - concentration), i.e., A*(c-A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth kinetics with a carrying capacity
- Rate independent of A (zero-order) → reaction limited by external factor such as catalyst surface saturation or light intensity
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel or competing reaction mechanisms
- Explicit time dependence in rate expression → non-autonomous system such as photochemical reactions, temperature ramps, or catalyst deactivation
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) → chain reaction mechanisms where radical intermediates follow half-order kinetics

**GT:** `-0.18997742423620262*A**2 + 0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

The second term is a rational function: `A²/(c*A⁴ + 1)`. Let me rewrite this as `A²/(c*A⁴ + 1)`.

Now I need to check each candidate to see if it can reproduce this form. The GT is a function of A only (no t dependence), so candidates with t can still work if t-dependent terms can be zeroed out.

The key structural requirement is: we need both a `-c*A²` term AND a rational term `A²/(d*A⁴ + 1)`.

Let me focus on candidates that could produce rational functions of A:
